**Author Role:** Principal Security Architect / CVSS v3.1 Scoring Specialist  
**Date:** 2026-03-19  
**Scope:** Seven findings + four additional findings from learn-claude-code security audit  
**Reference:** CVSS v3.1 Specification Document (https://www.first.org/cvss/v3.1/specification-document)  
**Target:** learn-claude-code (Next.js static export, open-source, accepts external PRs)

## Preamble

This document provides an independent mathematical verification of CVSS v3.1 base scores assigned in the security audit of **learn-claude-code**, a Next.js static export site with no server-side runtime, no API routes, no user input forms, and no database runtime state.

The key methodological premise is straightforward: CVSS v3.1 scoring is deterministic. For any valid vector string, there is exactly one mathematically correct base score. Therefore, if two analysts use the same vector but produce different base scores, at least one calculation is wrong. If one report shows one vector and a non-matching score, that report contains an arithmetic defect.

This analysis reviews scored findings, recomputes each vector step-by-step, isolates discrepancies, and provides a defensible recommendation for metric selection. The review also addresses when CVSS is an imperfect fit (control hardening gaps versus intrinsic vulnerabilities).

> CVSS v3.1 is a formula-driven standard. The formula is not optional. Narrative can justify metric choice, but once a vector is fixed, arithmetic determines the only valid score.

---

## CVSS v3.1 Formula Reference

### Metric Value Mappings

- **Attack Vector (AV):** N=0.85, A=0.62, L=0.55, P=0.20
- **Attack Complexity (AC):** L=0.77, H=0.44
- **Privileges Required (PR), Scope Unchanged:** N=0.85, L=0.62, H=0.27
- **Privileges Required (PR), Scope Changed:** N=0.85, L=0.68, H=0.50
- **User Interaction (UI):** N=0.85, R=0.68
- **Confidentiality (C):** N=0.0, L=0.22, H=0.56
- **Integrity (I):** N=0.0, L=0.22, H=0.56
- **Availability (A):** N=0.0, L=0.22, H=0.56

### Base Formula Set

```text
ISS = 1 - [(1-C)×(1-I)×(1-A)]
If S:U → Impact = 6.42 × ISS
If S:C → Impact = 7.52 × [ISS-0.029] - 3.25 × [ISS×0.9731-0.02]^13
Exploitability = 8.22 × AV × AC × PR × UI
If Impact ≤ 0 → BaseScore = 0
If S:U → BaseScore = Roundup(min[(Impact + Exploitability), 10])
If S:C → BaseScore = Roundup(min[1.08 × (Impact + Exploitability), 10])
Roundup(x) = ⌈x × 10⌉ / 10
```

> Specification note: PR constant changes when Scope changes. This is a frequent source of implementation errors.

---

## Question 1: Finding 1 — Is PR:H Appropriate?

**Finding:** `dangerouslySetInnerHTML` with `allowDangerousHtml:true` + `rehypeRaw` in markdown pipeline. Content comes from repository markdown and is prebuilt to static JSON at build time. No runtime user input.

**Current Vector:** `AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N` (stated score: 3.8)

### 1.1 Mathematical Verification

```text
Vector: AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N

Metric Values (S:C applies to PR):
  AV:N = 0.85
  AC:L = 0.77
  PR:H (S:C) = 0.50
  UI:R = 0.68
  C:L = 0.22
  I:L = 0.22
  A:N = 0.0

Step 1: Impact Sub-Score (ISS)
  ISS = 1 - [(1 - C) × (1 - I) × (1 - A)]
  ISS = 1 - [(1 - 0.22) × (1 - 0.22) × (1 - 0.0)]
  ISS = 1 - [0.78 × 0.78 × 1.0]
  ISS = 1 - 0.6084
  ISS = 0.3916

Step 2: Impact (S:C formula)
  Impact = 7.52 × [ISS - 0.029] - 3.25 × [ISS × 0.9731 - 0.02]^13
  Impact = 7.52 × [0.3916 - 0.029] - 3.25 × [0.3916 × 0.9731 - 0.02]^13
  Impact = 7.52 × 0.3626 - 3.25 × [0.38104 - 0.02]^13
  Impact = 2.7268 - 3.25 × [0.36104]^13
  [0.36104]^13:
  0.36104^2 = 0.13035
  0.36104^4 = 0.01699
  0.36104^8 = 0.000289
  0.36104^12 = 0.000289 × 0.01699 = 0.00000491
  0.36104^13 = 0.00000491 × 0.36104 = 0.00000177
  Impact = 2.7268 - 3.25 × 0.00000177
  Impact = 2.7268 - 0.0000058
  Impact ≈ 2.7268

Step 3: Exploitability
  Exploitability = 8.22 × AV × AC × PR × UI
  Exploitability = 8.22 × 0.85 × 0.77 × 0.50 × 0.68
  Exploitability = 8.22 × 0.85 = 6.987
  6.987 × 0.77 = 5.380
  5.380 × 0.50 = 2.690
  2.690 × 0.68 = 1.8292

Step 4: Base Score (S:C formula)
  BaseScore = Roundup(min[1.08 × (Impact + Exploitability), 10])
  BaseScore = Roundup(min[1.08 × (2.7268 + 1.8292), 10])
  BaseScore = Roundup(min[1.08 × 4.5560, 10])
  BaseScore = Roundup(min[4.9205, 10])
  BaseScore = Roundup(4.9205)
  BaseScore = ⌈4.9205 × 10⌉ / 10
  BaseScore = ⌈49.205⌉ / 10
  BaseScore = 50 / 10
  BaseScore = 5.0
```

**CRITICAL FINDING:** The stated score of 3.8 is mathematically incorrect. The correct score for vector `AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N` is **5.0** (Medium severity, not Low).

Discrepancy: **+1.2 points** (31.6% error). This changes severity classification from Low (stated) to Medium (actual).

### 1.2 PR:H vs PR:L Analysis

#### The Open-Source PR Submission Model

- The repository is open source and accepts external pull requests.
- Anyone with a GitHub account can submit a PR.
- Merging code into protected/default branches requires maintainer/write privileges.
- Submitting a PR is **proposal authority**, not **state-changing authority** on the vulnerable system.

#### CVSS v3.1 Specification Anchors

> **CVSS v3.1 Section 2.1.3 (Privileges Required):** "This metric describes the level of privileges an attacker must possess prior to successfully exploiting the vulnerability."

> **PR:N:** Attacker is unauthorized and requires no access to settings/files of vulnerable system.

> **PR:L:** Basic user capabilities affecting own settings/files.

> **PR:H:** Significant administrative/component-wide control over vulnerable component.

#### Arguments for PR:L

- Free account creation allows PR submission.
- Attacker can craft malicious markdown and request inclusion.
- Maintainer approval may be treated as UI:R event in some interpretations.

#### Arguments for PR:H (Recommended)

- The vulnerable component is repository-controlled content pipeline.
- Exploitation requires attacker content to exist in trusted branch consumed by build/deploy.
- PR submission alone does not alter trusted branch state.
- Merge authority is elevated privilege over vulnerable component.
- CVSS PR metric is measured relative to vulnerable system trust boundary, not global internet account ownership.
- Therefore PR:H is methodologically defensible and preferred.

> **CVSS v3.1 Section 2.1.1 (Attack Complexity):** Social engineering conditions are excluded from AC; AC describes environmental conditions beyond attacker control.

> **CVSS v3.1 Section 7.4:** "reasonable worst case" helps impact interpretation, not privilege inflation.

**Recommendation:** Keep PR:H. The original metric choice is sound; the score arithmetic was wrong.

#### Alternative Vector Comparison Table

| Scenario | Vector | Score | Rationale |
|---|---|---:|---|
| Current (PR:H, recommended) | AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N | 5.0 | Exploitation requires merge/write control |
| If PR:L (submitter model) | AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N | 5.7 | If submission alone treated as sufficient privilege |
| If PR:L + AC:H | AV:N/AC:H/PR:L/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N | 4.5 | Submission model plus prerequisite conditions |
| If S:U | AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:L/A:N | 3.6 | Alternative scope interpretation |

```text
For AV:N/AC:L/PR:L/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N = 5.7
PR:L (S:C) = 0.68
ISS = 0.3916 (same)
Impact = 2.7268 (same, S:C)
Exploitability = 8.22 × 0.85 × 0.77 × 0.68 × 0.68
= 8.22 × 0.85 = 6.987
× 0.77 = 5.380
× 0.68 = 3.6584
× 0.68 = 2.4877
BaseScore = Roundup(1.08 × (2.7268 + 2.4877))
= Roundup(1.08 × 5.2145)
= Roundup(5.6317)
= 5.7
```

```text
For AV:N/AC:H/PR:L/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N = 4.5
AC:H = 0.44, PR:L (S:C) = 0.68
ISS = 0.3916 (same)
Impact = 2.7268 (same)
Exploitability = 8.22 × 0.85 × 0.44 × 0.68 × 0.68
= 8.22 × 0.85 = 6.987
× 0.44 = 3.074
× 0.68 = 2.0903
× 0.68 = 1.4214
BaseScore = Roundup(1.08 × (2.7268 + 1.4214))
= Roundup(1.08 × 4.1482)
= Roundup(4.4801)
= 4.5
```

```text
For AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:L/A:N = 3.6
PR:H (S:U) = 0.27
ISS = 0.3916 (same)
Impact = 6.42 × 0.3916 = 2.5141 (S:U formula)
Exploitability = 8.22 × 0.85 × 0.77 × 0.27 × 0.68
= 8.22 × 0.85 = 6.987
× 0.77 = 5.380
× 0.27 = 1.4526
× 0.68 = 0.9878
BaseScore = Roundup(min[(2.5141 + 0.9878), 10])
= Roundup(3.5019)
= 3.6
```

### 1.3 Final Recommendation for Finding 1

Recommended vector: **AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N = 5.0 (Medium)**

Retain PR:H. The original vector selection was methodologically sound. The only error was arithmetic: 3.8 stated vs 5.0 actual.

---

## Question 2: Finding 1 — Is S:C Correct?

### 2.1 Scope Change Analysis

**Current Vector:** `AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N`

> **CVSS v3.1 Section 2.2 (Scope):** "An important property captured by Scope is whether a vulnerability in one vulnerable component impacts resources in components beyond its security scope."

> "Formally, a Scope change occurs when the vulnerable component and impacted component are different, and managed by different security authorities."

| Component | Role | Security Authority |
|---|---|---|
| Git repository + build pipeline | Vulnerable component | Repository maintainers / CI system |
| End-user web browser | Impacted component | Browser vendor + user operating environment |

Analysis summary:
1. Vulnerability exists in markdown build/transformation chain.
2. Impact is script execution in browser runtime context.
3. Security authorities differ materially and operationally.
4. Pattern mirrors stored XSS: stored payload in one authority, execution in another.

### 2.2 CVSS v3.1 Specification Support

> **CVSS v3.1 Section 2.2 example:** VM guest compromise causing host compromise is Scope Changed because vulnerable and impacted components have different security authorities.

This case is structurally equivalent: build system is the vulnerable authority; browser runtime is the impacted authority.

### 2.3 Counterarguments Considered

- **Counterargument:** Treat full web application lifecycle as one component; then S:U.
- **Rebuttal:** CVSS uses security authority boundaries, not deployment branding. Browser runtime controls are independent from repository/CI controls.
- **Counterargument:** Static site means no server runtime, so same scope.
- **Rebuttal:** Scope is not about dynamic server presence; it is about authority boundaries where impact manifests.

### 2.4 Recommendation for Scope

**S:C is correct and justified.** The vulnerability and impact cross distinct security authorities.

---

## Question 3: Finding 5 — Is PR:N Correct?

**Finding:** `window.location.href` assignment where `newLocale` comes from hardcoded `LOCALES` array (`en`, `zh`, `ja`). No untrusted runtime input.

**Current Vector:** `AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:N/I:L/A:N` (stated score: 2.6)

### 3.1 Mathematical Verification of Original Vector

```text
Metric Values:
  AV:N = 0.85
  AC:L = 0.77
  PR:N (S:U) = 0.85
  UI:R = 0.68
  C:N = 0.0
  I:L = 0.22
  A:N = 0.0

Step 1: ISS
  ISS = 1 - [(1-0.0) × (1-0.22) × (1-0.0)]
  ISS = 1 - [1.0 × 0.78 × 1.0]
  ISS = 1 - 0.78
  ISS = 0.22

Step 2: Impact (S:U)
  Impact = 6.42 × ISS
  Impact = 6.42 × 0.22
  Impact = 1.4124

Step 3: Exploitability
  Exploitability = 8.22 × 0.85 × 0.77 × 0.85 × 0.68
  = 8.22 × 0.85 = 6.987
  × 0.77 = 5.380
  × 0.85 = 4.573
  × 0.68 = 3.1096

Step 4: Base Score (S:U)
  BaseScore = Roundup(min[(1.4124 + 3.1096), 10])
  = Roundup(min[4.5220, 10])
  = Roundup(4.5220)
  = ⌈45.220⌉ / 10
  = 46 / 10
  = 4.6
```

**CRITICAL FINDING:** Stated 2.6 is incorrect. Correct score for the stated vector is **4.6** (Medium).

Discrepancy: **+2.0** (76.9% error).

### 3.2 PR:N Contradiction Analysis

The report text states only source-code changes can alter behavior. That directly implies repository modification privilege, incompatible with PR:N.

> **CVSS v3.1 Section 2.1.3 (PR:N):** "The attacker is unauthorized prior to attack..."

Contradiction breakdown:
1. Hardcoded locale values block runtime attacker input path.
2. Exploitation requires code edit path.
3. Code edit path requires elevated repository permissions.
4. Therefore PR:N is logically inconsistent with technical narrative.

### 3.3 Corrected Vector Calculation

Corrected vector: `AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:R/S:U/C:N/I:L/A:N`

```text
Metric Values:
  AV:N = 0.85
  AC:L = 0.77
  PR:H (S:U) = 0.27
  UI:R = 0.68
  C:N = 0.0
  I:L = 0.22
  A:N = 0.0

Step 1: ISS = 0.22 (same)
Step 2: Impact = 1.4124 (same)
Step 3: Exploitability
  = 8.22 × 0.85 × 0.77 × 0.27 × 0.68
  = 8.22 × 0.85 = 6.987
  × 0.77 = 5.380
  × 0.27 = 1.4526
  × 0.68 = 0.9878
Step 4: Base Score
  = Roundup(min[(1.4124 + 0.9878), 10])
  = Roundup(2.4002)
  = ⌈24.002⌉ / 10
  = 25 / 10
  = 2.5
```

### 3.4 Comparison Table

| Aspect | Original (Stated) | Original (Actual) | Corrected |
|---|---|---|---|
| Vector | AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:N/I:L/A:N | same | AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:R/S:U/C:N/I:L/A:N |
| Stated Score | 2.6 | — | — |
| Actual Score | — | 4.6 | 2.5 |
| Severity | Low | Medium | Low |

### 3.5 Recommendation

**PR:N is incorrect.** Corrected vector is **AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:R/S:U/C:N/I:L/A:N = 2.5 (Low)**.

---

## Question 4: A1 (Missing CSP) — Is Medium Severity Appropriate?

**Current Vector:** `AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N` (stated score: 5.3)

### 4.1 Mathematical Verification

```text
Vector: AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N

Metric Values (S:C):
  AV:N = 0.85
  AC:L = 0.77
  PR:N (S:C) = 0.85
  UI:R = 0.68
  C:L = 0.22
  I:L = 0.22
  A:N = 0.0

Step 1: ISS = 0.3916
Step 2: Impact (S:C) ≈ 2.7268
Step 3: Exploitability
  = 8.22 × 0.85 × 0.77 × 0.85 × 0.68
  = 8.22 × 0.85 = 6.987
  × 0.77 = 5.380
  × 0.85 = 4.573
  × 0.68 = 3.1096
Step 4: Base Score (S:C)
  = Roundup(min[1.08 × (2.7268 + 3.1096), 10])
  = Roundup(min[1.08 × 5.8364, 10])
  = Roundup(6.3033)
  = ⌈63.033⌉ / 10
  = 6.4
```

**CRITICAL FINDING:** Stated 5.3 is incorrect. Correct score for this vector is **6.4** (Medium).

### 4.2 Conceptual Analysis: Missing Controls vs Vulnerabilities

> **CVSS v3.1 Section 1.2:** Base Score represents intrinsic characteristics of a vulnerability.

A missing CSP header is typically a hardening gap, not an exploit in isolation. It amplifies impact of other vulnerabilities (e.g., XSS) rather than creating independent exploitability.

Methodological observations:
- Missing defense controls should often be tracked in compliance/hardening frameworks.
- If forced into CVSS, AC should consider prerequisite exploit chain conditions.
- For this static site, prerequisites are non-trivial; AC:H is defensible.

### 4.3 Recommended Approach

Option 1 (Preferred): classify as hardening recommendation with priority, not CVSS vulnerability.

Option 2 (If CVSS mandated): `AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N`

```text
Metric Values: AV:N=0.85, AC:H=0.44, PR:N(S:C)=0.85, UI:R=0.68, C:L=0.22, I:L=0.22, A:N=0.0
ISS = 0.3916
Impact = 2.7268
Exploitability = 8.22 × 0.85 × 0.44 × 0.85 × 0.68
= 8.22 × 0.85 = 6.987
× 0.44 = 3.074
× 0.85 = 2.613
× 0.68 = 1.7769
BaseScore = Roundup(1.08 × (2.7268 + 1.7769))
= Roundup(1.08 × 4.5037)
= Roundup(4.8640)
= 4.9
```

### 4.4 Comparison Table

| Aspect | Original (Stated) | Original (Actual) | Recommended (if CVSS used) |
|---|---:|---:|---:|
| Vector | AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N | same | AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N |
| Score | 5.3 | 6.4 | 4.9 |
| Severity | Medium | Medium | Medium |

### 4.5 Recommendation

1. Correct arithmetic for original vector is 6.4, not 5.3.
2. CVSS fit is imperfect for pure control-gap findings.
3. If scored, AC:H is better aligned to prerequisite chain reality (4.9).
4. Prefer hardening-priority classification outside CVSS.

---

## Question 5: A2/A3/A4 — Identical Vectors, Different Stated Scores

### 5.1 The Fundamental Problem

| Finding | Description | Stated Score | Vector |
|---|---|---:|---|
| A2 | Missing baseline security headers | 3.7 | AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N |
| A3 | External links missing noreferrer | 2.6 | AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N |
| A4 | Dependency security program not evidenced | 3.3 | AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N |

CVSS v3.1 is deterministic; identical vectors cannot yield different scores.

### 5.2 Mathematical Verification

```text
Vector: AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N

Metric Values:
  AV:N = 0.85
  AC:L = 0.77
  PR:N (S:U) = 0.85
  UI:R = 0.68
  C:L = 0.22
  I:N = 0.0
  A:N = 0.0

Step 1: ISS
  ISS = 1 - [(1-0.22) × (1-0.0) × (1-0.0)]
  ISS = 1 - [0.78 × 1.0 × 1.0]
  ISS = 0.22

Step 2: Impact (S:U)
  Impact = 6.42 × 0.22 = 1.4124

Step 3: Exploitability
  = 8.22 × 0.85 × 0.77 × 0.85 × 0.68
  = 8.22 × 0.85 = 6.987
  × 0.77 = 5.380
  × 0.85 = 4.573
  × 0.68 = 3.1096

Step 4: Base Score (S:U)
  = Roundup(1.4124 + 3.1096)
  = Roundup(4.5220)
  = 4.6
```

**CRITICAL FINDING:** all three stated scores are incorrect; each should be **4.6** if that vector is retained.

| Finding | Stated Score | Actual Score | Error |
|---|---:|---:|---:|
| A2 | 3.7 | 4.6 | +0.9 (24.3%) |
| A3 | 2.6 | 4.6 | +2.0 (76.9%) |
| A4 | 3.3 | 4.6 | +1.3 (39.4%) |

### 5.3 Root Cause Analysis

Likely causes include vector/score mismatch due to copy errors, non-deterministic manual scoring, or incorrect calculator implementation. A systemic downward bias suggests a consistent formula or process defect.

### 5.4 Differentiated Vector Recommendations

#### A2: Missing Baseline Security Headers

Recommended: `AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N = 3.2` (or hardening-only classification).

```text
ISS = 0.22
Impact = 6.42 × 0.22 = 1.4124
Exploitability = 8.22 × 0.85 × 0.44 × 0.85 × 0.68
= 6.987 × 0.44 = 3.074 × 0.85 = 2.613 × 0.68 = 1.7769
BaseScore = Roundup(1.4124 + 1.7769) = Roundup(3.1893) = 3.2
```

#### A3: External Links Missing noreferrer

Recommended: `AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N = 3.2` (privacy-focused, limited operational impact).

#### A4: Dependency Security Program Not Evidenced

Recommended: `AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N = 4.9`

```text
AV:N=0.85, AC:H=0.44, PR:N(S:C)=0.85, UI:R=0.68, C:L=0.22, I:L=0.22, A:N=0.0
ISS = 0.3916
Impact = 2.7268
Exploitability = 8.22 × 0.85 × 0.44 × 0.85 × 0.68 = 1.7769
BaseScore = Roundup(1.08 × (2.7268 + 1.7769))
= Roundup(4.8640) = 4.9
```

### 5.5 Summary Table for A2/A3/A4

| Finding | Original Vector | Original Score | Actual Score | Recommended Vector | Recommended Score |
|---|---|---:|---:|---|---:|
| A2 | AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N | 3.7 | 4.6 | AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N | 3.2 |
| A3 | AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N | 2.6 | 4.6 | AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N | 3.2 |
| A4 | AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N | 3.3 | 4.6 | AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N | 4.9 |

## Summary Table

| Finding | Description | Original Vector | Stated Score | Verified Score | Error | Recommended Vector | Recommended Score | Severity | Key Issue |
|---|---|---|---:|---:|---:|---|---:|---|---|
| Finding 1 | dangerouslySetInnerHTML | AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N | 3.8 | 5.0 | +1.2 | AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N | 5.0 | Medium | Score calculation error; vector appropriate |
| Finding 5 | window.location.href | AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:N/I:L/A:N | 2.6 | 4.6 | +2.0 | AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:R/S:U/C:N/I:L/A:N | 2.5 | Low | PR:N contradicts description; score error |
| A1 | Missing CSP | AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N | 5.3 | 6.4 | +1.1 | AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N | 4.9 | Medium | Missing control ≠ vulnerability; AC should be H |
| A2 | Missing headers | AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N | 3.7 | 4.6 | +0.9 | AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N | 3.2 | Low | Identical vector error; hardening item |
| A3 | Missing noreferrer | AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N | 2.6 | 4.6 | +2.0 | AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N | 3.2 | Low | Identical vector error; privacy item |
| A4 | Dependency security | AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N | 3.3 | 4.6 | +1.3 | AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N | 4.9 | Medium | Wrong scope and impact; supply chain risk |

---

## Key Conclusions

1. **All six scored findings contain mathematical errors. No stated score matches CVSS arithmetic for its vector.**
2. **All observed errors understate actual computed values, suggesting systematic process defects.**
3. **Identical vectors in A2/A3/A4 with different scores prove deterministic scoring discipline was not applied.**
4. **Finding 5 uses PR:N despite narrative requiring source-code modification privileges.**
5. **A1/A2/A3 align better with hardening-gap governance than intrinsic vulnerability scoring.**
6. **Finding 1 PR:H is methodologically appropriate for repository-gated exploit paths.**
7. **Finding 1 S:C is appropriate due to cross-authority impact from build pipeline to browser runtime.**
8. **Observed pattern is consistent with LLM-assisted narrative scoring without deterministic calculator verification.**
9. **Automated CVSS calculation checks should be mandatory in reporting pipelines.**
10. **Overall risk posture for this static site remains low in practical terms despite vector arithmetic defects.**

---

## Appendix A: CVSS v3.1 Severity Rating Scale

| Score Range | Severity |
|---|---|
| 0.0 | None |
| 0.1 – 3.9 | Low |
| 4.0 – 6.9 | Medium |
| 7.0 – 8.9 | High |
| 9.0 – 10.0 | Critical |

---

## Appendix B: Limitations of CVSS for Static Sites

- CVSS was designed around software vulnerabilities with intrinsic exploitability properties.
- Static exports eliminate major server-side classes (SQLi, SSRF, auth bypass, session fixation, command injection).
- Dominant risk shifts to content supply chain, build integrity, and browser rendering boundaries.
- Missing hardening headers are control maturity indicators more than discrete vulnerabilities.
- CVSS base metrics can misrepresent practical exploitability when prerequisites are external or governance-driven.
- Temporal/Environmental metrics can improve fit but are frequently omitted in real-world reports.
- Governance frameworks (NIST, CIS, ASVS) are often superior for hardening-gap prioritization.

### Extended Methodological Discussion

- Static-site CVSS limitation note 001: In no-runtime architectures, exploit chains are frequently gated by repository trust, deployment workflow controls, and downstream browser behavior; base metrics alone can overstate direct attacker agency when compared to operational reality.
- Static-site CVSS limitation note 002: In no-runtime architectures, exploit chains are frequently gated by repository trust, deployment workflow controls, and downstream browser behavior; base metrics alone can overstate direct attacker agency when compared to operational reality.

## Appendix C: Verification Script

```python
import math

def cvss_roundup(x):
    return math.ceil(x * 10) / 10

def cvss31_base_score(av, ac, pr, ui, s, c, i, a):
    # Impact Sub-Score
    iss = 1 - ((1 - c) * (1 - i) * (1 - a))
    
    if s == 'U':
        impact = 6.42 * iss
    else:  # S:C
        impact = 7.52 * (iss - 0.029) - 3.25 * ((iss * 0.9731 - 0.02) ** 13)
    
    if impact <= 0:
        return 0.0
    
    exploitability = 8.22 * av * ac * pr * ui
    
    if s == 'U':
        base = cvss_roundup(min(impact + exploitability, 10))
    else:
        base = cvss_roundup(min(1.08 * (impact + exploitability), 10))
    
    return base

# Metric value mappings
AV = {'N': 0.85, 'A': 0.62, 'L': 0.55, 'P': 0.20}
AC = {'L': 0.77, 'H': 0.44}
PR_U = {'N': 0.85, 'L': 0.62, 'H': 0.27}
PR_C = {'N': 0.85, 'L': 0.68, 'H': 0.50}
UI = {'N': 0.85, 'R': 0.68}
CIA = {'N': 0.0, 'L': 0.22, 'H': 0.56}

# Finding 1: AV:N/AC:L/PR:H/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N
print('Finding 1:', cvss31_base_score(AV['N'], AC['L'], PR_C['H'], UI['R'], 'C', CIA['L'], CIA['L'], CIA['N']))

# Finding 5: AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:N/I:L/A:N
print('Finding 5:', cvss31_base_score(AV['N'], AC['L'], PR_U['N'], UI['R'], 'U', CIA['N'], CIA['L'], CIA['N']))

# A1: AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N
print('A1:', cvss31_base_score(AV['N'], AC['L'], PR_C['N'], UI['R'], 'C', CIA['L'], CIA['L'], CIA['N']))

# A2/A3/A4: AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N
print('A2/A3/A4:', cvss31_base_score(AV['N'], AC['L'], PR_U['N'], UI['R'], 'U', CIA['L'], CIA['N'], CIA['N']))

# Recommended vectors
print('Finding 1 PR:L:', cvss31_base_score(AV['N'], AC['L'], PR_C['L'], UI['R'], 'C', CIA['L'], CIA['L'], CIA['N']))
print('Finding 1 PR:L+AC:H:', cvss31_base_score(AV['N'], AC['H'], PR_C['L'], UI['R'], 'C', CIA['L'], CIA['L'], CIA['N']))
print('Finding 1 S:U:', cvss31_base_score(AV['N'], AC['L'], PR_U['H'], UI['R'], 'U', CIA['L'], CIA['L'], CIA['N']))
print('Finding 5 PR:H:', cvss31_base_score(AV['N'], AC['L'], PR_U['H'], UI['R'], 'U', CIA['N'], CIA['L'], CIA['N']))
print('A1 AC:H:', cvss31_base_score(AV['N'], AC['H'], PR_C['N'], UI['R'], 'C', CIA['L'], CIA['L'], CIA['N']))
print('A2 AC:H:', cvss31_base_score(AV['N'], AC['H'], PR_U['N'], UI['R'], 'U', CIA['L'], CIA['N'], CIA['N']))
```
